  44. UPDATE - DECEMBER 2015 - After my review update of April, this trimmer went downhill decisively, and yet maddingly random and sporadic. Frankly it's been driving me nuts for 8 months. I have been SO busy with other things that addressing this faulty trimmer had not been at the top of my list, so continued to make me CRAZY. When I plug the charger cord into the trmmer, pushing the plug all the way in DOES NOT solve the problem as it seemed to briefly. The LED was flashing randomly with the charger plugged in, more or less corresponing to wiggling it, SOMETIMES, the LED would not light at all -- seeming to indicate the plug is not making contact and it's not charging. THEN, WHEN I REMOVED THE CHARGER PLUG, THE TRIMMER TURNED ON! Truly bizarre. Never has it just charged normally when I plugged it in. Also, several times when I plugged the charger plug in, the trimmer it went on! It would appear that the electronic control cirucuit on these trimmers are defective (many other reviews showing similar symptoms). This is going from 4 stars to one, and I will contact Wahl's customer service to see what happens. I see from reviews that some customers received a replacement which also had the same problem. Clearly I was overly hasty to give this product a good review, given the downhill experience since I bought and reviewed it. (Don't review this kind of product so soon after you buy it.) (PREVIOUS) UPDATE - APRIL 2015 - When I plugged the charging cord into the shaver, the light indicating that it charging was flickering randomly and I discovered that the &quot;charging&quot; indicator light when on and off when moving the plug and socket where it plugs into the shaver --- seeming to mean that there's a bad connection inside the socket inside the clipper body. I was planning on calling the company and returning it, but didn't get around to it. HOWEVER, I THEN REALIZED THAT I WASN'T PUSHING THE PLUG ALL THE WAY INTO THE SOCKET. APPARENTLY YOU MUST PUSH IT IN WITH SOME FORCE, UNTIL IT CLICKS INTO PLACE. After I discovered that and was careful to push it in hard all the way it seemed to be OK. I've been otherwise happy with it, because it gets the job done. However another minor complaint is that the design of the body isn't very ergonomically efficeint --- the designer probably didn't use a focus group, etc. It is a simple, univorm very smooth (slipery) shape, and since it's exactly the same on all sides, you cannot tell by feel which side is which. Assuming I'll keep this and not return it, I'm likely to cover the body, possibly with that mesh rubber shelf liner stuf that has a strong gripping friction. This will allow a more secure grip on the clipper. (End of April 2015 update) Original reveiw: This is well worth the additional cost. I have power tools and know well the benefits of lithium-ion battery power. (Good lithium-ion power tools are expensive, but one truly doesn't regret having paid it, very much worth the cost --- tons of power for the weight and very durable.) I bought this to replace a rechargeable Wahl that had a special rechargeable Ni-cad battery, and it seemed to cut in and out (fast, slow fast slow) very irritating, I tried everything possible to fix it, and nothing worked. It seemed like a junk toy that way. To be fair, I didn't oil the cutter regularly, which maybe many users fail to do, and possibly may have made some difference. I'm going to try to lube this one regularly with mineral oil, available inexpensively from any drugstore. This kind of clipper should be lubed on a regular baisis. In summary, it seems surprising that any company sells such junk and at the same time also sells the very best available quality products, which this clipper clearly is.

  74. Wahl has bucked the race to the bottom trend of cheap plastic toys disguised as trimmers with the release of the 9818. The first thing that sets this trimmer apart from the others, is the quality of workmanship. This American made, yes - American made trimmer , has a solid, stainless steel body that feels heavy, in a good way. Unlike the Wahl &#34;All-In-One Lithium Ion&#34; model's blades, the 9818 blades are made of stainless steel - keeping them rust resistant. The shaver attachment is now a single, thinner foil, reducing potential blind spots, making it more accurate for lining and tapering. The motor is relatively quiet, yet consistently powered. For the holder, Wahl has replaced the impractical, all-inclusive blade and shaver rack stand with a singular, molded, piece of frosted plastic for a base - which has the exclusivity of a plastic water bottle but - IT WORKS, as I actually use it. The shaver fits snugly, and takes up little space near the sink, without the clutter. Now for some of the drawbacks: The shaver cannot be used while charging - not a big deal as the led light flashes when the battery is low, there is a &#34;quick charge&#34;, and the battery, when fully charged - lasts relatively long. The t-blade (especially on the newer models) aren't sharp enough to give you that clean type beard and moustache lining you get from a barbershop type trimmer, without multiple attempts. The attachable blade guides could have been more precise for stubble and shorter lengths. Overall - still a good effort by Wahl. Hopefully, it will send a message that amid the sea of mediocrity in men's trimmers, many men will spend a few dollars more for a well designed and better made trimmer.

Spacing between blade teeth is farther away and, well, just not very accurate when you look. The competitor's packages look nice, but all one gets is another disposable product in the end. The products work for a while when given the chance, but the following year, it's time to buy a new one. Why keep adding to your local landfill?<br /><br />I've been using a corded Wahl for so long that I thought my trimmer was reaching the end of its useful life. It still cuts, don't get me wrong, but not like it used to. Sure, I could purchase some replacement blades, but I really wanted an excuse to buy a new trimmer. Plus, my trimmer blades don't operate as fast as new when moving back and forth. And yes, I use oil.<br /><br />Boy, I was so excited to find that Wahl was making a stainless lithium ion version! Normally, I wouldn't go for a rechargeable trimmer because they just don't perform like a corded version, not to mention, rechargeable products only take so many charges over their lifetime and then they become disposable. Furthermore, they take forever to charge and just don't seem to last very long on a charge. With the invention of lithium ion batteries, this just isn't the case, anymore. Not only is lithium ion capable of hundreds of charges more, but it doesn't take long to reach a full charge and lasts way longer when charged. Discharging when idle doesn't happen as quickly either. What's not to like about that? It's almost a no brainer. Almost.<br /><br />So I purchased a Wahl Lithium Ion+. Before I even used it, I came here and read some reviews to see what others had to say. I didn't want to believe the bad reviews. Heck, even the most perfect product will have some naysayers, right? On the other hand, there were so many positive reviews. Enough to seem to give the product an overwhelmingly good average. Surely, all those positive reviews couldn't be wrong. Enough, I thought, I just need to try it out myself...<br /><br />You can imagine my disappointment when I encountered problems charging the trimmer unit right off the bat. Bad first impression. Seems the plug on the cord at the trimmer end doesn't really make a positive connection with the single pin at the bottom of the trimmer. You shove it in there, but then when you go to lay it down on your counter, this connection slips and there goes your power and the blue indicator light goes out. I shoved it back in hoping I missed the click lock, but there isn't one. Are you kidding? For this kind of money Wahl cannot come up with a better connection than that?! Even modern radar detector connectors found a way to overcome this faulty, failure of a single pin connection. Come on!!! I manage to maintain a connection and get it to charge for a few moments so that I can try it out. I didn't find it noisy, as others mentioned. In fact, it was kind of quiet. The weight felt good in my hand and it seemed to trim like past Wahl products. I go to plug it back in, as it wasn't fully charged and then I find myself having to shove the power adapter into the bottom forcefully again to make sure it has a connection. This is when I became fed up. I boxed it back up and returned it the next day.<br /><br />I would really steer clear of this until Wahl makes some necessary improvements. Hopefully, one such improvement is with the charger interface. Until then, I might have to check out a Braun.

They come on and off easily--and don't collect much dirt/hairs. I was surprised how easy it was to keep the attachments clean. The attachments are stable and mounts solidly.<br /><br />The stainless steel handle feels very quality, balanced feel in the hand. Also keeps clean with a simple wipe of the thumb. The reviewer having problems with the power button: the trick is to let go of the switch completely after turning it on, before turning it off again. The switch does not \\"double-tap\\".<br /><br />I much prefer how this entire package simplifies and down-sizes the groomer system: I appreciate that the charger is as small as possible, with no wasted plastic stand. For travel, this entire system fits in a - as far as I know - the smallest package of any competitors. Using a trimmer without a cord is a superior experience, and will hopefully put many more barber shops out of business!

It typically lasts me about 3 months on a charge, since I tend to &#34;train&#34; batteries by running them thru 3 full charge/discharge cycles when they're new (and this is the last of those 3 cycles, new charge + 3 more). An old habit I got into that may not be relevant for current battery types, yet still seems to serve me well in conditioning the batteries for long life. And yes, this Wahl gives me an extended span of usage per charge, especially when compared to all the older models I used to have. I trim for ~15 minutes each week, plus the occasional touch-up, and I get about 3 months per charge.<br /><br />Attachments? Plenty of them - more than you'll need. Now, some folks whose review I read before buying have dinged this groomer for having too many attachments. Not valid, really; if you don't need 'em, don't use 'em. The fact is, Wahl gives you plenty of OPTIONS for you to choose from! Find the ones which are most useful to you and stash the rest - simple! I haven't changed the head from the blade to another blade, or the nose hair trimmer (yet), but I will - I just haven't gotten the urge to do so. As for the combs, I tried a bunch of them and finally settled on two that I use every week; first the longer one, then the shorter one. Works perfectly and gives me a neat, well-groomed look in an easier, FASTER fashion than I've ever been able to accomplish before. I've even had multiple comments on how nicely trimmed my beard is, but only after I started using the Wahl 9818. :-)<br /><br />The other complaint isabout the plastic stand. Pshaw, people, what do you want, a really good trimmer, or an overpriced stand on which to place said trimmer? I'll take the first, thank you. Yes, it's a plain, clear plastic stand that is 100% functional and just the right size. They designed it to hold your trimmer in the same position, allowing it to be plugged in or not, as needed. If it's plugged in, you can easily see the charge light as it stands there, so you know that it's done when the light goes out. Works perfectly, unobtrusive, and because it's not unnecessarily fancy, they didn't have to up the price to cover anything you didn't need.<br /><br />BOTTOM LINE: This trimmer is worth every penny! I am completely and totally happy that I bought it, I love its style, form, & functionality, and I'd buy it again in a heartbeat if I needed another one.about the plastic stand. The solid metal body is comfortable & all the various clipper heads seem well-designed & work perfectly.<br /><br />I especially like that it's American made; the body is stainless steel; the T-blade, & all the blades are stainless steel & are easily removable; the other heads interchange easily; the rotary nose trimmer performs better than my Panasonic unit; the LED on the on/off button indicates when it's charging & starts blinking when the battery is low; the multiple trimmer guides provide a wide selection regarding closeness of trim; & the motor is relatively quiet & performs very well. I'm able to get a neat, precise, & accurate trim.<br /><br />What I don't like is that the shaver cannot be used while charging - not a big deal as the led light flashes when the battery is low, there is a &#34;quick charge&#34;, & the battery, when fully charged - seems to lasts a relatively long time. The battery should be replaceable. The trimmer guides could have been made out of a little better grade of plastic. Another annoyance is the little plastic plug that's in the base when you receive it, don't lose it - you'll need that for traveling to prevent the trimmer from turning on & draining your lithium ion battery - I had to retrieve it out of the recycling bin after reading the manual!<br /><br />The pluses more than outweigh the minuses and thanks to all the reviews I read I knew about them before the purchase, so still give it 5 stars. The Wahl 9818 is well designed & built. I was looking for a better trimmer & it seems I've found it. If you have any kind of arthritis you may find it difficult or painful to operate.<br /><br />The smooth stainless body requires a firm grip since it has no rubber or molded protrusions to make it easier to hold, but I expected that from the picture.<br /><br />One nice thing is that the accessories from other similar sized trimmers fit, so you can buy the rotary head, small bladed detail trimmer, etc and they will all fit.<br /><br />And of course it's 120/240v, so if you travel that's a good thing.<br /><br />All in all I don't hate it, but I really would like to have loved it more, especially at this price.
